     <p>The <b>University of California, Irvine</b> (<b>UCI</b>, <b>UC Irvine</b>, or <b>Irvine</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Irvine,_California" title="Irvine, California">Irvine, California</a> and one of the 10 general campuses in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> (UC) <a href="/wiki/University_system" title="University system">system</a>. UCI's <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a> campus is the fifth-largest in the UC system, with over 28,000 students, 1,100 faculty members and 9,000 staff.</p> 
     <p>UC Irvine is considered a <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a> and offers 80 undergraduate degrees and 98 graduate and professional degrees. The university is designated as having <a href="/wiki/List_of_research_universities_in_the_United_States" title="List of research universities in the United States">very high research activity</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education</a>, and in 2009 had $325.49 million in <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> expenditures according to the National Science Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> UC Irvine became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> in 1996, and is the youngest university to hold membership.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also administers the <a href="/wiki/UC_Irvine_Medical_Center" title="UC Irvine Medical Center">UC Irvine Medical Center</a>, a large <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">teaching hospital</a>; the UC Irvine Health Sciences system in the <a href="/wiki/Orange,_California" title="Orange, California">City of Orange</a>; the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Irvine,_Arboretum" title="University of California, Irvine, Arboretum" class="mw-redirect">University of California, Irvine, Arboretum</a>; and a portion of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California_Natural_Reserve_System" title="University of California Natural Reserve System">University of California Natural Reserve System</a>.</p> 
     <p>UCI was one of three new UC campuses established in the 1960s to accommodate growing enrollments across the UC system. A site in Orange County was identified in 1959, and in the following year <a href="/wiki/The_Irvine_Company" title="The Irvine Company" class="mw-redirect">The Irvine Company</a> sold the University of California 1,000 acres (400&nbsp;ha) of land <a href="/wiki/Nominal_consideration" title="Nominal consideration" class="mw-redirect">for one dollar</a> to establish the new campus. President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> dedicated the campus in 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/UC_Irvine_Anteaters" title="UC Irvine Anteaters">UC Irvine Anteaters</a> compete in 18 men's and women's sports in the <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">NCAA Division I</a> as members of the <a href="/wiki/Big_West_Conference" title="Big West Conference">Big West Conference</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Pacific_Sports_Federation" title="Mountain Pacific Sports Federation">Mountain Pacific Sports Federation</a>. Since 1969, the university has won 28 national team championships in nine different sports and has had 63 individual national champions.</p>

          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of California, Irvine was one of three new campuses established in the 1960s under the <a href="/wiki/California_Master_Plan_for_Higher_Education" title="California Master Plan for Higher Education">California Master Plan for Higher Education</a> with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Diego" title="University of California, San Diego">San Diego</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Santa_Cruz" title="University of California, Santa Cruz">Santa Cruz</a> campuses.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> During the 1950s, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> saw the need for the new campuses to handle both the large number of college-bound World War II veterans (largely due to the <a href="/wiki/G._I._Bill_of_Rights" title="G. I. Bill of Rights" class="mw-redirect">G. I. Bill</a>) and the expected increase in enrollment from the <a href="/wiki/Post-World_War_II_baby_boom" title="Post-World War II baby boom" class="mw-redirect">post-war baby boom</a>. One of the new campuses was to be in the Los Angeles area; the location selected was Irvine Ranch, an area of agricultural land bisecting <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a> from north to south. This site was chosen to accommodate the county's growing population, complement the growth of nearby <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a> and <a href="/wiki/UC_Riverside" title="UC Riverside" class="mw-redirect">UC Riverside</a>, and allow for the construction of a master planned community in the surrounding area.<sup id="cite_ref-site_selection_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-site_selection-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UCISign.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/UCISign.jpg/220px-UCISign.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/UCISign.jpg/330px-UCISign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e9/UCISign.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UCISign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> One of two identical UCI signs that face the main campus' western entrance.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Unlike most other University of California campuses, UCI was not named for the city it was built in; at the time of the university's founding (1965), the current city of <a href="/wiki/Irvine,_CA" title="Irvine, CA" class="mw-redirect">Irvine</a> (established in 1975) did not exist. The name &quot;Irvine&quot; is a reference to <a href="/wiki/James_Irvine_(landowner)" title="James Irvine (landowner)">James Irvine</a>, a landowner who administered the 94,000-acre (38,000&nbsp;ha) Irvine Ranch. In 1960, <a href="/wiki/The_Irvine_Company" title="The Irvine Company" class="mw-redirect">The Irvine Company</a> sold 1,000 acres (400&nbsp;ha) of the Irvine Ranch to the University of California for one dollar, since a company policy prohibited the donation of property to a public entity.<sup id="cite_ref-site_selection_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-site_selection-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The University purchased an additional 510 acres (210&nbsp;ha) in 1964 for housing and commercial developments. Much of the land that was not purchased by UCI (which is now occupied by the cities of Irvine, <a href="/wiki/Tustin,_California" title="Tustin, California">Tustin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newport_Beach,_California" title="Newport Beach, California">Newport Beach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Newport_Coast,_Newport_Beach,_California" title="Newport Coast, Newport Beach, California" class="mw-redirect">Newport Coast</a>) is now held under <a href="/wiki/The_Irvine_Company" title="The Irvine Company" class="mw-redirect">The Irvine Company</a>. During this time, the University also hired <a href="/wiki/William_Pereira" title="William Pereira">William Pereira</a> and Associates as the Master Planner of the Irvine Ranch area. Pereira intended for the UC Irvine campus to complement the neighboring community, and the two grew in tandem. Soon after UC Irvine opened in 1965, the City of Irvine became incorporated and established in 1971 and 1975, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-site_selection_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-site_selection-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC Irvine's first Chancellor, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_G._Aldrich" title="Daniel G. Aldrich">Daniel G. Aldrich</a>, developed the campus' first academic plan around a College of Arts, Letters, and Science, a Graduate School of Administration, and a School of Engineering. The College of Arts, Letters, and Science was composed of twenty majors in five &quot;Divisions&quot;: Biological Sciences, Fine Arts, Humanities, Physical Sciences, and Social Sciences (which transformed into the present-day &quot;Schools&quot;).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Aldrich was also responsible for implementing the wide variety of flora and fauna on the campus that fit the local Mediterranean climate zone, feeling that it served an &quot;aesthetic, environmental, and educational [purpose].&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:LyndonBJohnsonUCIrvineGroundbreaking1964.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/LyndonBJohnsonUCIrvineGroundbreaking1964.jpg/220px-LyndonBJohnsonUCIrvineGroundbreaking1964.jpg" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/LyndonBJohnsonUCIrvineGroundbreaking1964.jpg/330px-LyndonBJohnsonUCIrvineGroundbreaking1964.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/LyndonBJohnsonUCIrvineGroundbreaking1964.jpg/440px-LyndonBJohnsonUCIrvineGroundbreaking1964.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:LyndonBJohnsonUCIrvineGroundbreaking1964.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> President 
        <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> at the university's groundbreaking ceremony in June 1964
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>On June 20, 1964, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> dedicated UC Irvine before a crowd of 15,000 people, and on October 4, 1965 the campus began operations with 1,589 students, 241 staff members, 119 faculty, and 43 teaching assistants.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> However, many of UCI's buildings were still under construction and landscaping was still in progress, with the campus only at 75% completion.<sup id="cite_ref-lib_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lib-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> By June 25, 1966, UCI held its first Commencement with fourteen students, which conferred ten Bachelors of Arts, three Masters of Arts, and one Doctor of Philosophy degree.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1965 the <a href="/w/index.php?title=California_College_of_Medicine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="California College of Medicine (page does not exist)">California College of Medicine</a> (originally a <a href="/wiki/Osteopathic_medicine_in_the_United_States" title="Osteopathic medicine in the United States">school of osteopathy</a> founded in 1896 and the oldest continuously operating medical college in the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">Southwest</a>) became part of UC Irvine.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-som.uci.edu_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-som.uci.edu-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1976, plans to establish an on-campus hospital were set aside, with the university instead purchasing the Orange County Medical Center (renamed the UC Irvine Medical Center) around 12 miles from UC Irvine, in the City of Orange.<sup id="cite_ref-som.uci.edu_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-som.uci.edu-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Present_day">Present day</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Present day">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Irvine_overhead.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Downtown_Irvine_overhead.jpg/220px-Downtown_Irvine_overhead.jpg" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Downtown_Irvine_overhead.jpg/330px-Downtown_Irvine_overhead.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Downtown_Irvine_overhead.jpg/440px-Downtown_Irvine_overhead.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Irvine_overhead.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A view of suburban 
        <a href="/wiki/Irvine,_California" title="Irvine, California">Irvine</a>. The white tower in the foreground is part of University Center, and everything to its left and right is part of UCI.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As the largest employer in <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a>, UCI contributes an annual economic impact of $4.2 billion with an operating budget of almost $1.9 billion for 2008 including $328 million in extramural research funding.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Numerous other educational and training opportunities are offered in numerous areas ranging from physician residency programs at UC Irvine's Medical Center to community certificate programs and other coursework through University Extension.</p> 
     <p>In 2011-2012, UC Irvine awarded 8,443 degrees: 6,766 <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degrees" title="Bachelor's degrees" class="mw-redirect">bachelor's degrees</a> 1,105 <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degrees" title="Master's degrees" class="mw-redirect">Master's degrees</a>, 413 <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">Ph.D.s</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Education" title="Doctor of Education">Ed.D.s</a>, 102 <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">M.D.s</a>, and 57 <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">J.D.s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_growth">Future growth</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Future growth">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>As a part of its long-term efforts to &quot;attain flagship status,&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> UC Irvine has implemented construction projects (estimated to cost $1.3 billion over the next decade) that will accelerate the campus build-out and employ the remainder of the university's land grant.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The exponential increase in construction activity is a part of the <i>Strategy for Academic Development at UCI through 2015</i>, a master plan that outlines the vision of making UCI a first-choice university for college applicants nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-evc.uci.edu_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evc.uci.edu-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> This increase also spawned a popular <a href="/wiki/Backronym" title="Backronym">backronym</a> of UCI: &quot;Under Construction Indefinitely.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Campus_of_the_University_of_California,_Irvine_(aerial_view,_circa_2006).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Campus_of_the_University_of_California%2C_Irvine_%28aerial_view%2C_circa_2006%29.jpg/220px-Campus_of_the_University_of_California%2C_Irvine_%28aerial_view%2C_circa_2006%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Campus_of_the_University_of_California%2C_Irvine_%28aerial_view%2C_circa_2006%29.jpg/330px-Campus_of_the_University_of_California%2C_Irvine_%28aerial_view%2C_circa_2006%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Campus_of_the_University_of_California%2C_Irvine_%28aerial_view%2C_circa_2006%29.jpg/440px-Campus_of_the_University_of_California%2C_Irvine_%28aerial_view%2C_circa_2006%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Campus_of_the_University_of_California,_Irvine_(aerial_view,_circa_2006).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> UCI's core campus and surrounding areas. Aldrich Park is in the center.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The layout of the core campus resembles a rough circle with its center being Aldrich Park, initially known as Central Park, and lined up by the Ring Mall and buildings surrounding the road. To further emphasize the layout, academic units are positioned relative to the center, wherein undergraduate schools are closer to the center than the graduate schools.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Aldrich Park is planted with over 11,120 trees (over 24,000 for the entire campus), including 33 species of eucalyptus. They planted two trees in 1990: one for Arbor Day and the second for Chancellor Daniel Aldrich who died that year. On September 11, 2002, the Chancellor planted a bay laurel tree in remembrance of the heroes and victims of September 11, 2001. The tree was a gift from the UCI Staff Assembly. The park is the site for ?Wayzgoose,? a medieval student festival held each year in conjunction with the ?Celebrate UCI? open house. There are also many extracurricular activities that can be done in the park.</p> 
     <p>Ring Mall is the main pedestrian road used by students and faculty to travel around the core campus. The road measures up to a perfect mile and completely encircles Aldrich Park.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Most schools and libraries are lined up by this road with each of these schools having their own central plaza which also connects to the Aldrich Park.</p> 
     <p>Other areas of the university outside of the core campus such as the School of Arts are connected by four pedestrian bridges. Beyond the core campus and the bridges, the layout of the campus is more suburban.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1098px;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner"> 
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Uci-park-pano.jpg" class="image" title="Panoramic view of Aldrich Park."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Uci-park-pano.jpg/1090px-Uci-park-pano.jpg" width="1090" height="160" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Uci-park-pano.jpg/1635px-Uci-park-pano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Uci-park-pano.jpg/2180px-Uci-park-pano.jpg 2x" /></a>
       </div> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uci-park-pano.jpg" title="Enlarge"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6b/Magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" /></a>
        </div> 
        <center>
         <i>Panoramic view of Aldrich Park.</i>
        </center> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Surroundings">Surroundings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Surroundings">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/UCI_Medical_Center" title="UCI Medical Center" class="mw-redirect">UCI Medical Center</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Irvine,_Arboretum" title="University of California, Irvine, Arboretum" class="mw-redirect">University of California, Irvine, Arboretum</a>,&nbsp;and 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_California_Natural_Reserve_System" title="University of California Natural Reserve System">University of California Natural Reserve System</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UCI_Anteater_sand_sculpture.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/UCI_Anteater_sand_sculpture.jpg/220px-UCI_Anteater_sand_sculpture.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/UCI_Anteater_sand_sculpture.jpg/330px-UCI_Anteater_sand_sculpture.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/UCI_Anteater_sand_sculpture.jpg/440px-UCI_Anteater_sand_sculpture.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UCI_Anteater_sand_sculpture.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Anteater sand sculpture.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UCI is close to beaches, mountains, and the attractions of Southern California. Although the campus is located in the city of <a href="/wiki/Irvine,_California" title="Irvine, California">Irvine</a>, it is located very close to the city of <a href="/wiki/Newport_Beach" title="Newport Beach" class="mw-redirect">Newport Beach</a>; in fact, the campus itself is directly bounded by the city of Newport Beach and <a href="/wiki/Newport_Coast" title="Newport Coast" class="mw-redirect">Newport Coast</a> on many sides. The western side of the campus borders the <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Joaquin_Freshwater_Marsh_Reserve&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Joaquin Freshwater Marsh Reserve (page does not exist)">San Joaquin Freshwater Marsh Reserve</a>, through which Campus Drive connects UCI to the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_405_(California)" title="Interstate 405 (California)">405 freeway</a>. The northern and eastern sides of UCI are adjacent to Irvine proper; the eastern side of the campus is delineated by Bonita Canyon Road, which turns into Culver Drive at its northern terminus and offers links to the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Route_73" title="California State Route 73">San Joaquin Hills Toll Road</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_405_(California)" title="Interstate 405 (California)">405 freeway</a>, respectively. Additionally, UCI's southern boundary is adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Route_73" title="California State Route 73">San Joaquin Transportation Corridor</a>.</p> 
     <p>There exists a &quot;North Campus&quot; that houses the Facilities Management Department, the Faculty Research Facility, Central Receiving, Fleet Services, the Air Pollution Health Effects Laboratory, and numerous other functions. It is located next to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Irvine,_Arboretum" title="University of California, Irvine, Arboretum" class="mw-redirect">UCI Arboretum</a>; both the North Campus and the arboretum are located about 1 mile (2&nbsp;km) from the main campus.</p> 
     <p>William Pereira's original street layout for the region surrounding the University had a <a href="/wiki/Nut_(hardware)" title="Nut (hardware)">wingnut</a>-shaped loop road as the main thoroughfare, which twice crossed the campus. However, the <a href="/wiki/Irvine_Company" title="Irvine Company">Irvine Company</a>'s development plans expanded before it could be completed, and portions of California, Carlson, Harvard and Turtle Rock roads today constitute segments of what would have been the Loop Road.</p> 
     <p>Despite the suburban environment, a variety of wildlife inhabits the University's central park, open fields, and wetlands. The university has <a href="/wiki/Bobcat" title="Bobcat">bobcats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_lion" title="Mountain lion" class="mw-redirect">mountain lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawk" title="Hawk">hawks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle" class="mw-redirect">golden eagles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_blue_heron" title="Great blue heron" class="mw-redirect">great blue herons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squirrel" title="Squirrel">squirrels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opossum" title="Opossum">opossums</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peregrine_falcon" title="Peregrine falcon" class="mw-redirect">peregrine falcons</a>, rabbits, <a href="/wiki/Raccoon" title="Raccoon">raccoons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Owl" title="Owl">owls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skunk" title="Skunk">skunks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weasel" title="Weasel">weasels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bat" title="Bat">bats</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coyote" title="Coyote">coyotes</a>. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Irvine,_Arboretum" title="University of California, Irvine, Arboretum" class="mw-redirect">UCI Arboretum</a> hosts a collection of plants from California and Mediterranean climates around the world. The small rabbits in particular are very numerous and can be seen across campus in high numbers, especially during hours of low student traffic.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Kriegerhall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Kriegerhall.jpg/220px-Kriegerhall.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Kriegerhall.jpg/330px-Kriegerhall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Kriegerhall.jpg/440px-Kriegerhall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Kriegerhall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Murray_Krieger" title="Murray Krieger">Murray Krieger</a> Hall in the School of Humanities, named after an inspirational professor and an example of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Brutalist" title="Brutalist" class="mw-redirect">Brutalist</a> architecture of the campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The first buildings were designed by a team of architects led by <a href="/wiki/William_Pereira" title="William Pereira">William Pereira</a> and including <a href="/wiki/A._Quincy_Jones" title="A. Quincy Jones">A. Quincy Jones</a> and William Blurock. The initial landscaping, including Aldrich Park, was designed by an association of three firms, including that of the noted urban-landscaping innovator Robert Herrick Carter. Aldrich Park was designed under the direction of landscape architect Gene Uematsu, and was modeled after <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Law_Olmsted" title="Frederick Law Olmsted">Frederick Law Olmsted</a>'s designs for New York City's <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a>. The campus opened in 1965 with the inner circle and park only half-completed. There were only nine buildings and a dirt road connecting the main campus to the housing units. Only three of the six &quot;spokes&quot; that radiate from the central park were built, with only two buildings each. Pereira was retained by the university to maintain a continuity of style among the buildings constructed in the inner ring around the park, the last of which was completed in 1972. These buildings were designed in a style which combined sweeping curves and expressionistic shapes with elements of classic California architecture such as red tiled roofs and clay-tiled walkways, and distinctive white railings evoking the deck of an ocean liner.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> These buildings featured an innovative structural design that freed the interiors from support columns in order to allow future alterations of their floor plans.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Engineering,UCI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Engineering%2CUCI.jpg/220px-Engineering%2CUCI.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Engineering%2CUCI.jpg/330px-Engineering%2CUCI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Engineering%2CUCI.jpg/440px-Engineering%2CUCI.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Engineering,UCI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Former Engineering Complex
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Construction on the campus all but ceased after the Administration building, Aldrich Hall, was completed in 1974, and then resumed in the late 1980s, beginning a massive building boom that still continues today. This second building boom continued the futuristic trend, but emphasized a much more colorful, <a href="/wiki/Postmodern" title="Postmodern" class="mw-redirect">postmodern</a> approach that somewhat contradicted the earthy, organic designs of the early buildings. Architects such as <a href="/wiki/Frank_Gehry" title="Frank Gehry">Frank Gehry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Venturi" title="Robert Venturi">Robert Venturi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Owen_Moss" title="Eric Owen Moss">Eric Owen Moss</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Stirling_(architect)" title="James Stirling (architect)">James Stirling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Erickson" title="Arthur Erickson">Arthur Erickson</a> were brought in to bring the campus more up to date. The recession in the early 1990s along with internal politics led to a change in direction, due to the reduced capital budget, and changing attitudes towards architectural innovation at the University. This in turn led to a &quot;contextualist&quot; approach beginning in the late 1990s combining stylistic elements of the first two phases in an attempt to provide an architectural &quot;middle ground&quot; between the two vastly different styles. Gehry's building was recently removed from campus to make way for a new building, with a design that has been called a &quot;big beige box with bands of bricks.&quot; In 2009 the Humanities Gateway building, designed by <a href="/wiki/Curtis_W._Fentress" title="Curtis W. Fentress">Curtis W. Fentress</a>, was opened. Its curvilinear design marked a return to the sculptural treatment of concrete begun by Pereira.</p> 
     <p>As of 2005, the campus has more than 200 buildings and encompasses most of the university's 1,525 acres (6.17&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-lib_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lib-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus is in the midst of a $1.1 billion construction campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries_and_study_centers">Libraries and study centers</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Libraries and study centers">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Irvine_campus#Libraries_and_study_centers" title="University of California, Irvine campus" class="mw-redirect">University of California, Irvine campus#Libraries and study centers</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UCILibrary.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/UCILibrary.jpg/220px-UCILibrary.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/UCILibrary.jpg/330px-UCILibrary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/UCILibrary.jpg/440px-UCILibrary.jpg 2x" /></a>

        <div class="magnify">

        </div> Langson Library is the main repository for most of UC Irvine's research materials and hosts many study areas. It is one of four central libraries maintained by UC Irvine.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UC_Irvine,_Science_Library.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/UC_Irvine%2C_Science_Library.JPG/220px-UC_Irvine%2C_Science_Library.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/UC_Irvine%2C_Science_Library.JPG/330px-UC_Irvine%2C_Science_Library.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/UC_Irvine%2C_Science_Library.JPG/440px-UC_Irvine%2C_Science_Library.JPG 2x" /></a>

     </table> 
     <p>UCI is noted for having many excellent special collections and archives. In addition to holding a noted <a href="/wiki/Critical_Theory" title="Critical Theory" class="mw-redirect">Critical Theory</a> archive and Southeast Asian archive, the Libraries also contain extensive collections in Dance and Performing Arts, Regional History, and more. Additionally, Langson Library hosts an extensive East Asian collection with materials in Chinese, Japanese, and Korean.</p> 
     <p>Nearly all departments and schools on campus complement the resources of the UC Irvine Libraries by maintaining their own reading rooms and scholarly meeting rooms. They contain small reference collections and are the choice for more intimate lectures, graduate seminars, and study sessions. There is also the large Gateway Study Center (across from Langson Library), one of the university's original buildings and under the custody of UC Irvine Libraries. Having served formerly as a cafeteria and student center, it is now a dual-use computer lab and study area which is open nearly 24 hours.</p> 
     <p>The UCI Student Center offers a large number of study areas, auditoriums, and two food courts and therefore is one of the most popular places to study on campus. UC Irvine also has a number of computer labs that serve as study centers. The School of Humanities maintains its Humanities Instructional Resource Center, a drop-in computer lab specializing in language and digital media. Additionally, UCI maintains five other drop-in labs, four instructional computer labs, and a number of reservation-only SmartClassrooms, some of which are open 24 hours. Other popular study areas include Aldrich Park, the Cross-Cultural Center, the Locus (a study room and computer lab used by the Campuswide Honors Program), and plazas located in every School.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tunnels">Tunnels</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tunnels">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>An underground network of tunnels runs between many of the major buildings on campus and the Central Plant, with the major trunk passage located beneath Ring Mall. Smaller tunnels branch off from this main passage to reach individual buildings, carrying electrical and air-conditioning utilities from the Central Plant. These tunnels have been the subject of much campus lore, the most popular story being that the tunnels were constructed to facilitate the safe evacuation of faculty in the event of a student riot. The main tunnel actually appears above ground in the form of an unusually thick bridge near the Engineering Tower, in an area where Ring Mall crosses between two hills.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Like other <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> campuses, UC Irvine is governed by a Chancellor who has significant authority over campus academic and planning affairs. The Chancellor, in turn, is nominated by and is responsible to the <a href="/wiki/Regents_of_the_University_of_California" title="Regents of the University of California">Regents of the University of California</a> and the UC President:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>1962 <a href="/wiki/Daniel_G._Aldrich" title="Daniel G. Aldrich">Daniel G. Aldrich</a></li> 
      <li>1984 <a href="/wiki/Jack_W._Peltason" title="Jack W. Peltason">Jack W. Peltason</a></li> 
      <li>1993 Laurel L. Wilkening</li> 
      <li>1998 <a href="/wiki/Ralph_J._Cicerone" title="Ralph J. Cicerone">Ralph J. Cicerone</a></li> 
      <li>2005 <a href="/wiki/Michael_V._Drake" title="Michael V. Drake">Michael V. Drake</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>After the Chancellor, the second most senior official is the Executive Vice Chancellor and Provost.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> He serves as the university's chief academic and operating officer. Every school on campus reports to the Executive Vice Chancellor and Provost through a Dean, and all other academic and administrative units report to his office through a Vice Chancellor or chief administrator. A partial list of these units includes Campus Recreation, Intercollegiate Athletics, Planning and Budget, Student Affairs, UC Irvine Libraries, UC Irvine Medical Center, and University Advancement. The Executive Vice Chancellor and Provost also governs the faculty senate.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:

     </div>

        </div> The School of Social Sciences from Aldrich Park.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UC Irvine's academic units are referred to as Schools. There are eight undergraduate Schools, two graduate Schools, one Department, and one field of Interdisciplinary Studies. The most recent academic unit, the College of Health Sciences, was established in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> On November 16, 2006, the UC Regents approved the establishment of the School of Law, which opened in fall 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The remaining academic units offer accelerated or community education in the form of Summer Session and UC Irvine Extension. Additionally, UCI's Campuswide Honors Program is implementing an independent study program, which will allow students to develop their own curriculum across Schools and graduate with their own self-created major.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Engineeringtower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Engineeringtower.jpg/220px-Engineeringtower.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Engineeringtower.jpg/330px-Engineeringtower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Engineeringtower.jpg/440px-Engineeringtower.jpg 2x" /></a>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_organizations">Research organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Research organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>To complement its mission as a research university, UCI hosts a diverse array of nationally and internationally-recognized research organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> These organizations are either chaired by or composed of UCI faculty, frequently draw upon undergraduates and graduates for research assistance, and produce a multitude of innovations, patents, and scholarly works. Some are housed in a school or department office; others are housed in their own multimillion-dollar facilities. These are a few of the more prolific research organizations at UCI:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Beckman Laser Institute</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/California_Institute_for_Telecommunications_and_Information_Technology" title="California Institute for Telecommunications and Information Technology">California Institute for Telecommunications and Information Technology</a> (Calit2)</li> 
      <li>Center for Complex Biological Systems</li> 
      <li>Center for Global Peace and Conflict Studies</li> 
      <li>Center for Cognitive Neuroscience</li> 
      <li>Center for Unconventional Security Affairs</li> 
      <li>Chao Family Comprehensive Cancer Center</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UC_Irvine_Institute_of_Transportation_Studies" title="UC Irvine Institute of Transportation Studies">Institute of Transportation Studies</a></li> 
      <li>National Fuel Cell Research Center</li> 
      <li>Reeve-Irvine Research Center</li> 
      <li>Center for the Study of Democracy</li> 
      <li>Center for Health Policy Research</li> 
      <li>W. M. Keck Center for Accelerator Mass Spectrometry</li> 
      <li>Sue and Bill Gross Stem Cell Research Center</li> 
     </ul>

     <p>UC Irvine is considered a <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a>. For 2012-2013, <i><a href="/wiki/US_News_%26_World_Report" title="US News &amp; World Report" class="mw-redirect">US News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked UC Irvine 44th among national universities and 12th among public universities in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, many of UCI's graduate programs consistently receive top-50 rankings from <i>US News &amp; World Report</i>, earning distinction in literary criticism and theory (1), criminology (5), creative writing (6), health care management (9), organic chemistry (11), information systems (11), physical chemistry (12), drama and theater (12), psychology-neurobiology and behavior (12), psychology ? cognitive science (16), theoretical chemistry (18), experimental psychology (19), cell biology/developmental biology (21), English (22), sociology (25), business-part-time (25), chemistry (26), computer science (28), aerospace engineering (29), psychology (29), mechanical engineering (30), physics (30), civil engineering (31), biological sciences (34), environmental engineering (34), political science (36), engineering (39), biomedical engineering (40), economics (42), history (42), mathematics (43), medicine-research (44), materials science engineering (45), psychology and social behavior (47), business (49), and electrical engineering (49).<sup id="cite_ref-today.uci.edu_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-today.uci.edu-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> in 2012 ranked UC Irvine 45th among all global universities, and 31st among all US universities.<sup id="cite_ref-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities-2012_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities-2012-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a></i> in 2012 ranked UC Irvine 4th among the top 100 global universities under 50 years old, and 1st among all US universities under 50 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_Higher_Education-100_under_50_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Higher_Education-100_under_50-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a></i> ranked UCI 16th out of the top 100 best-value public colleges and universities in the nation, and 5th in California.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">The Daily Beast</a></i> in 2010, quality of life is what students most value ?besides academics? and UCI ranked 16th among ?The 100 Happiest Colleges.?<sup id="cite_ref-The_100_Happiest_Colleges_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_100_Happiest_Colleges-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> In April 2013 CBS News MoneyWatch listed UCI as the 11th happiest public university, based on the greatest percentage of freshmen who remain for their sophomore year.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_faculty_and_Nobel_Laureates">Notable faculty and Nobel Laureates</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Notable faculty and Nobel Laureates">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uc_irvine8300001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Uc_irvine8300001.jpg/220px-Uc_irvine8300001.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Uc_irvine8300001.jpg/330px-Uc_irvine8300001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Uc_irvine8300001.jpg/440px-Uc_irvine8300001.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uc_irvine8300001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Reines" title="Frederick Reines">Frederick Reines</a> Hall in the School of Physical Sciences, named after one of three UCI faculty members to receive the 
        <a href="/wiki/Nobel_prize" title="Nobel prize" class="mw-redirect">Nobel prize</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Calit2,_UCI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Calit2%2C_UCI.jpg/220px-Calit2%2C_UCI.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Calit2%2C_UCI.jpg/330px-Calit2%2C_UCI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Calit2%2C_UCI.jpg/440px-Calit2%2C_UCI.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Calit2,_UCI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Calit2" title="Calit2" class="mw-redirect">Calit2</a>, UCI
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Three faculty members have been named <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a> recipients.<sup id="cite_ref-faculty_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faculty-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, three researchers from UCI's faculty received the Nobel Prize during their tenure at UCI: <b><a href="/wiki/Frank_Sherwood_Rowland" title="Frank Sherwood Rowland">Frank Sherwood Rowland</a></b> (<a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Chemistry</a>, 1995), <b><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Reines" title="Frederick Reines">Frederick Reines</a></b> (<a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Physics</a>, 1995), and <b><a href="/wiki/Irwin_Rose" title="Irwin Rose">Irwin Rose</a></b> (<a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Chemistry</a>, 2004). Dr. Rowland's Nobel-winning research was conducted exclusively at UC Irvine, along with fellow prize-winner <a href="/wiki/Mario_J._Molina" title="Mario J. Molina">Mario J. Molina</a>. Irwin Rose received the Nobel Prize for his work on biological proteins. F. Sherwood Rowland helped to discover the harmful effects of <a href="/wiki/Chlorofluorocarbon" title="Chlorofluorocarbon">CFCs</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">ozone layer</a>, while Frederick Reines received the Nobel Prize for his work in discovering the <a href="/wiki/Neutrino" title="Neutrino">neutrino</a>. UCI is the first public university to have two Nobel laureates (Rowland and Reines) who received their prizes in the same year (1995).</p> 
     <p><b><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Keneally" title="Thomas Keneally">Thomas Keneally</a></b> was a visiting professor at UCI where he taught the graduate fiction workshop for one quarter in 1985. From 1991 to 1995, he was a visiting professor in the writing program at UCI.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> He is most famous for his book <a href="/wiki/Schindler%27s_Ark" title="Schindler's Ark">Schindler's Ark</a> (1982) (later republished as <i>Schindler's List</i>), which won the Booker Prize and is the basis of the film <a href="/wiki/Schindler%27s_List" title="Schindler's List">Schindler's List</a> that was directed by <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>.</p> 
     <p>In January 2009, UCI Professor <b>Reg Penner</b> won the <a href="/wiki/Faraday_Medal" title="Faraday Medal">Faraday Medal</a> for his research with <a href="/wiki/Nanowires" title="Nanowires" class="mw-redirect">nanowires</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Henry W. Sobel</b> was awarded the Bruno Pontecorvo Prize in 2009 by the Joint Institute for Nuclear Research (JINR)in Dubna, Russia for his work on Neutrino Oscillations.</p> 
     <p>Evolutionary Biologist <b>Francisco Ayala</b> received the 2010 Templeton Prize for exceptional contribution to affirming life's spiritual dimension.</p>

     <p>UC Irvine is categorized by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> as &quot;more selective&quot; for college admissions ratings within the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> It is the fourth-most selective <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> campus, as measured by the ratio of admitted students to applicants (behind <a href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley" title="UC Berkeley" class="mw-redirect">UC Berkeley</a>, <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a>, and <a href="/wiki/UC_San_Diego" title="UC San Diego" class="mw-redirect">UC San Diego</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> UC Irvine received 56,525 applications for admission to the Fall 2012 incoming freshman class; 23,947 were admitted (42.46%).<sup id="cite_ref-AdmissionProfile_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AdmissionProfile-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Fall 2012 admitted freshman applicants had an average high school GPA of 4.02, an average ACT Composite score of 27, and an average combined SAT score of 1844 (average SAT scores of 588 for Critical Reading, 645 for Mathematics, and 611 for Writing).<sup id="cite_ref-AdmissionProfile_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AdmissionProfile-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The choice to offer admission is based on the University of California's comprehensive review program. It considers a candidate's personal situation, community involvement, extracurricular activities, and academic potential in addition to the traditional high school academic record, personal statement, and entrance examination scores.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> While residency is not a factor in admission, it is a factor in tuition expenses, with out-of-state residents spending more annually than California residents. State law prohibits UC Irvine from practicing <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a> in its admissions process.</p> 
     <p>For fall of 2012, the incoming freshman were predominately from <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County" title="Los Angeles County" class="mw-redirect">Los Angeles County</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area" title="Bay Area" class="mw-redirect">Bay Area</a> counties, <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riverside_County" title="Riverside County" class="mw-redirect">Riverside County</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Bernardino_County" title="San Bernardino County" class="mw-redirect">San Bernardino County</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_County" title="San Diego County" class="mw-redirect">San Diego County</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_County" title="Imperial County" class="mw-redirect">Imperial County</a>. The most popular major for freshmen is a major in Biological Sciences (20.6%), followed by Engineering (16.6%), Undecided/Undeclared (16.5%), Social Sciences (13.4%), Physical Sciences (8.0%), Humanities (5.2%), Business (4.4%), Information and Computer Sciences (3.8%), Social Ecology (3.1%), Arts (2.8%), Pharmaceutical Sciences (2.8%), Health Sciences (1.5%), Other (1.0%), and Nursing (0.4%).<sup id="cite_ref-freshman_profile_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freshman_profile-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Student_activities_and_traditions_at_UC_Irvine" title="Student activities and traditions at UC Irvine">Student activities and traditions at UC Irvine</a>
     </div> 
     <p>UCI's history as part of a preplanned suburban community, combined with the tendency for some students to go home on the weekends, gives Irvine a reputation as a quieter college town or a commuter school. However, there are a number of opportunities for vibrant and exciting social outings, as long as students take the initiative and have access to an automobile. In fact, most of the students live on or around campus. There are also many storied traditions at UCI, which have helped the young university develop a strong sense of campus spirit and personality.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UCI's Greek Life began in 1973 with three sororities (Delta Gamma, Pi Beta Phi, and Gamma Phi Beta) and three fraternities (Beta Theta Pi, Sigma Chi, and Phi Delta Theta).<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Today it is a very active and growing community, with over 2,200 students in 26 sororities and 21 fraternities representing a wide range of ethnicities, cultures, and backgrounds.</p> 
     <p>There are three major overhead bodies on the campus that govern Greek Life, Inter Fraternity Council, The Panhellenic Association, and The Multicultural Greek Council. The IFC governs over the thirteen chapters which are considered Greek by the National Inter Fraternity Council (NIC). The Panhellenic Association has ten NPC (National Panhellenic Conference) chapters and two local chapters. The Panhellenic community was recently opened up for expansion in Fall 2008, where they welcome Sigma Kappa to the campus. The Multicultural Greek Council was first established in 2009, where MGC currently governs 20 Multicultural Greek Chapters.</p> 
     <p>Major events and programs in the Greek Community include Songfest, All Greek Conference, Greek Week, BANG (Being a New Greek), and risk management programs (topics vary).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fraternities_and_sororities">Fraternities and sororities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Fraternities and sororities">edit</a>]</span></h4>
