     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clubs_and_organizations">Clubs and organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Clubs and organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>With over 550 student clubs and organizations on campus, students can readily find friends who share their interests whether academic, multicultural, political, religious, service, social, or athletic. Campus activities throughout the year include cultural nights, arts performances, live music at Anteater Plaza?special events such as Reggaefest, the Rainbow Festival, Wayzgoose Fair, Shocktoberfest, Earth Day ? and that?s just to name a few.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> The Psi chapter of <a href="/wiki/Phrateres" title="Phrateres">Phrateres</a>, a non-exclusive, non-profit social-service club, was installed here in 1967. Between 1924 and 1967, 23 chapters of Phrateres were installed in universities across North America.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residential_accommodations">Residential accommodations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Residential accommodations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Middleearth_dorms,_UCI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Middleearth_dorms%2C_UCI.jpg/220px-Middleearth_dorms%2C_UCI.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Middleearth_dorms%2C_UCI.jpg/330px-Middleearth_dorms%2C_UCI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Middleearth_dorms%2C_UCI.jpg/440px-Middleearth_dorms%2C_UCI.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Middleearth_dorms,_UCI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Residence Halls at the 
        <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle Earth</a> undergraduate housing complex (for freshmen) are named after places and characters from 
        <a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">J. R. R. Tolkien</a>'s 
        <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> book series.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Student_housing_at_UC_Irvine" title="Student housing at UC Irvine" class="mw-redirect">Student housing at UC Irvine</a>
     </div> 
     <p>UC Irvine has a number of residential options for students interested in living on campus. Approximately 36% of UCI students are housed in university accommodations; 3,300 live in freshmen residential dormitories, approximately 4,000 other undergraduates live in apartment/theme community housing, and 1,542 living units are available for graduate students and their families.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Part of UCI's long-range development plan involves expanding on-campus housing to accommodate 50% of all UCI students.<sup id="cite_ref-evc.uci.edu_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evc.uci.edu-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The on-campus housing communities for undergraduates are: Mesa Court, Middle Earth, Campus Village, Arroyo Vista, Vista Del Campo, and VDC Norte. Graduate students are able to live on campus in Palo Verde, Verano Place, Vista Del Campo, and VDC Norte.</p> 
     <p>As of Fall 2010, UCI?s on-campus housing will expand to include two new properties managed by American Campus Communities (the same management that operates Vista del Campo and VDC Norte). These new properties include Camino del Sol and Puerta del Sol. Camino del Sol is solely for undergraduate students, while Puerta del Sol can accommodate undergraduate and graduate students.</p> 
     <p>Mesa Court is a housing community for freshmen. Mesa Court was the first housing community at UCI, has many trees and plants, a volleyball court and 2 basketball courts. Students living in Mesa Court have a mandatory meal plan, and can eat at the Mesa Commons. Mesa Court also has a community center, a recreational center, and the Mesa Academic Center(MAC). The housing community is crossing the bridge from the Arts to Humanities, or crossing the street towards the Student Center.</p> 
     <p>The Middle Earth housing community is home to about 1,700 students. The community comprises 24 halls, two dining facilities (Brandywine and Pippin Commons), a student center, and several resource centers. The name of each building is named after J.R.R. Tolkien's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">The Hobbit</a></i> and <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>. Middle Earth was built in three phases. The first phase was built in 1974 with the opening of seven halls: Hobbiton, Isengard, Lorien, Mirkwood, Misty Mountain, Rivendell, and The Shire, along with a separate Head Resident's manufactured home called &quot;Bag End&quot;. The second phase was built in 1989 with thirteen more halls: Balin, Harrowdale, Whispering Wood, Woodhall, Calmindon, Grey Havens, Aldor, Rohan, Gondolin, Snowbourn, Elrond, Shadowfax, and Quenya. And finally, the third phase was built in 2000 with four halls: Crickhollow, Evenstar, Oakenshield, and Valimar. Each hall houses about fifty to eighty students. The hall Quenya was built with sixty single suite rooms and mainly houses graduate students. The hall Rivendell was originally opened as a co-ed, Social Science student dorm. Special, for credit, Social Science courses (&quot;Self and Community&quot; and &quot;Search for Community&quot;) were held in Rivendell. Later, Rivendell became a single gender suite for women; however, in Fall 2009, the hall has again become coed and the all-women's hall has been moved to Oakenshield hall. In Fall 2012, Rivendell became a single gender hall for men.</p> 
     <p>There are 42 houses located in Arroyo Vista and in use. There are 9 sorority and 5 fraternity houses that are located in Arroyo Vista. The sorority houses are Alpha Phi, Delta Delta Delta, Delta Gamma, Gamma Phi Beta, Pi Beta Phi, Alpha Chi Omega, Kappa Kappa Gamma, Sigma Kappa, and Kappa Alpha Theta. The fraternities in Arroyo Vista are Sigma Phi Epsilon, Sigma Chi, Phi Gamma Delta, Kappa Sigma, and Sigma Alpha Epsilon. Some of the themed houses include the Rosa Parks House, Casa Caesar Chavez, International Peace and Conflict Studies, and International Village. Arroyo Vista also has many academic themed houses such as Campuswide Honors Program, Engineering, Information and Computer Science, Humanities, and Social Ecology, and has two Second Year Experience Program houses. In 2010, Arroyo Vista opened three new theme houses: Spectrum, Culinary, and Sustainability House.</p> 
     <p>Before the 2009?2010 school year, Arroyo Vista housed first, second, third, fourth, and fifth-year undergraduates all in the same community. Beginning Fall 2009, however, Arroyo Vista does not house first years. As of Fall 2012, Arroyo Vista started the &quot;First Year Experience&quot; and now houses first year students within six of their houses. Students living in Arroyo Vista live in complexes that may be called houses, but have dorm-like qualities. Within each house, Arroyo Vista provides a kitchen area, laundry room, and a general living room. For instance, there are House Assistants (HA) present, who serve as the role as Resident Advisors (RA) and the rooms are all doubles. AV does not provide a meal plan within their housing contract, but a voluntary meal plan through UCI Dining can be purchased. Vista del Campo and Vista del Campo Norte are just up the road from AV, and are apartment-style, but are still run by UCI, so there are still many regulations and C.A.'s make rounds at night daily. VDC Norte, or simply &quot;Norte&quot; for short, has single rooms and double rooms for undergraduates; one common layout in an apartment in Norte has one double and two singles to an apartment. VDC has single rooms for undergraduates in the form of single, double, triple, or quad room occupancy with shared bathrooms in one apartment. To address the growing needs of housing and promote more on-campus house, UCI decided to open another apartment style housing for undergraduates called Camino Del Sol. Camino Del Sol provides single rooms, as well as a pool, community center, and fitness center. In fall 2012, Camino del Sol opened up housing to incoming first year students as an option besides dorm living. There are now apartments in Camino del Sol that house first year students that have opted for an apartment instead of living in the dorms on campus. For each housing community, ASUCI provides shuttles to allow students to travel between their housing site and campus. The wait for each bus can range around 7?10&nbsp;minutes; this allows fast transfer to the UCI campus.</p> 
     <p>Off-campus housing options vary widely, given a student's preferred living arrangements and budget. However, a common denominator for off-campus apartment housing in <a href="/wiki/Irvine,_California" title="Irvine, California">Irvine</a> and nearby <a href="/wiki/Newport_Beach,_California" title="Newport Beach, California">Newport Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tustin,_California" title="Tustin, California">Tustin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Costa_Mesa,_California" title="Costa Mesa, California">Costa Mesa</a> is the fact that most accommodations are maintained by <a href="/wiki/The_Irvine_Company" title="The Irvine Company" class="mw-redirect">The Irvine Company</a>. UCI offers off-campus housing search assistance and roommate listings through its student housing office.</p> 
     <p>Gender-neutral and <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> housing will be offered to students at UC Irvine beginning Fall 2010. These new housing options are inclusive to all students and may be a big step towards equality in the community. For first-years, the ?Open House? dorm will be located in Isengard in Middle Earth. The Open House will be a non-judgmental space where the diversity of identities and gender expressions are celebrated. It will provide opportunities for personal development to flourish in a gender-free and transgender-friendly living environment. This gender-neutral hall allows for both same and opposite gender roommate pairings. For continuing students, the ?Spectrum House? in Arroyo Vista will also be available as well. The community welcomes the cultural experiences for lesbian, gay, bisexual, transgender, intersex, queer, questioning students and their allies.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uci_sign.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Uci_sign.jpg/220px-Uci_sign.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Uci_sign.jpg/330px-Uci_sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Uci_sign.jpg/440px-Uci_sign.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uci_sign.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A prominent UCI sign at Crawford Hall, part of the Crawford Athletic Complex.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UCIrvineAnteaters.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/46/UCIrvineAnteaters.png/220px-UCIrvineAnteaters.png" width="220" height="301" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/46/UCIrvineAnteaters.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/46/UCIrvineAnteaters.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UCIrvineAnteaters.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> UC Irvine Anteaters logo
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/UC_Irvine_Anteaters" title="UC Irvine Anteaters">UC Irvine Anteaters</a>
     </div> 
     <p>UCI's sports teams are known as the <a href="/wiki/Anteaters" title="Anteaters" class="mw-redirect">Anteaters</a> and the student body is known as Antourage, decided in 2010?2011. They participate in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>'s Division I, as members of the <a href="/wiki/Big_West_Conference" title="Big West Conference">Big West Conference</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Pacific_Sports_Federation" title="Mountain Pacific Sports Federation">Mountain Pacific Sports Federation</a>. Their traditional rivals are <a href="/wiki/California_State_University,_Fullerton" title="California State University, Fullerton">Cal State Fullerton</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_State_University,_Long_Beach" title="California State University, Long Beach">Long Beach State</a>, and <a href="/wiki/UC_Santa_Barbara" title="UC Santa Barbara" class="mw-redirect">UC Santa Barbara</a>.</p> 
     <p>UCI fields nationally-competitive teams in cross country, track and field, basketball, baseball, volleyball, water polo, and soccer. UCI's renowned baseball program recently returned to UCI, after a period of state funding crises led to its temporary retirement.</p> 
     <p>UCI has won 28 national team championships in nine different sports since 1969 and has had 63 individual national champions. The most recent NCAA Division I national title was won by the men's volleyball team on May 4, 2013 against BYU (3?0) at Pauley Pavilion (UCLA) in Los Angeles. Other national titles include three other Division I men's volleyball titles, three Division I men's water polo titles, two baseball Division II titles, three men's swimming titles (Div. II), and six men's tennis titles (Div. II). The 2007 men's baseball team impressed the nation, the Anteaters being one of the Final Four teams left in the College World Series, just six years after the baseball program had been formally re-instated after a ten-year absence. The week of April 20, 2009 was a historical milestone for the UCI athletics program, as both school?s Men?s Volleyball and Baseball squads were simultaneously ranked No. 1 nationally in NCAA Division I polls. This marked the first time ever that UCI possessed two teams ranked No. 1 in the nation, as Baseball garnered the ranking based on Baseball America and Collegiate Baseball polls, while Men?s Volleyball earned the top spot on the American Volleyball Coaches Association (AVCA) poll.</p> 
     <p>More than 400 UCI student-athletes have earned All-America distinction, and Anteater teams have captured 66 conference championships. Since 1983, 3,266 UCI student-athletes have earned conference scholar-athlete awards. <sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_anteater_as_mascot">The anteater as mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: The anteater as mascot">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uci_mascot.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Uci_mascot.jpg/220px-Uci_mascot.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Uci_mascot.jpg/330px-Uci_mascot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Uci_mascot.jpg/440px-Uci_mascot.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uci_mascot.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The UCI mascot is the 
        <a href="/wiki/Anteater" title="Anteater">anteater</a>. This 430-pound statue is a gift of the class of 1987.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The anteater was chosen in 1965 when students were allowed to submit mascot candidates, which would be voted on in a campus election. Three undergraduates named Pat Glasgow, Bob Ernst, and Schuyler Hadley Basset III were credited with choosing the anteater and designing a cartoon representation, having been disappointed with other mascots such as a roadrunner, unicorn, seahawk and golden bison.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The original anteater design was not based not on the <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Hart" title="Johnny Hart">Johnny Hart</a> comic strip, &quot;<a href="/wiki/B.C._(comic_strip)" title="B.C. (comic strip)">B.C.</a>&quot; but on a somewhat less wholesome symbol ? the Playboy bunny.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 1965, the UCI students officially voted on the anteater, and many embraced their far-out mascot. In a special follow-up election, students opted for a mascot based on the B.C. anteater over the Playboy version. Since it was &quot;original and slightly irrelevant,&quot; it became the mascot of UC Irvine after winning 56% of the vote, beating a close second with the choice of &quot;none of the above&quot;. The anteaters are not to be confused with the aardvark, an African animal that also eats ants. The anteater has grown to become a beloved mascot, and is the inspiration for many of UCI's <a href="/wiki/UC_Irvine_Anteaters" title="UC Irvine Anteaters">athletic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Student_Activities_and_Traditions_at_UC_Irvine" title="Student Activities and Traditions at UC Irvine" class="mw-redirect">campus spirit</a> traditions.</p> 
     <p>Since the return of baseball in 2002 (the sport was eliminated in 1992 due to state budget cuts), UC Irvine has been ranked as high as No. 1 in the country in 2009, and has been at the top of the Big West Conference standings, which is considered by some to be one of the top Division I Baseball Conferences outside the major conferences in the country. In June 2007, the UC Irvine baseball team participated in the College World Series for the first time ever in school history. The Anteaters shocked the nation, and made Series history, becoming the first team to ever win two extra-inning College World Series games back-to-back, by beating (and eliminating) Cal State Fullerton (5?4, F/13), followed by nationally ranked Arizona State (8?7, F/10), only to lose their next game to defending National Champions, and well rested, Oregon State, having played a record 31 innings in three days to finish in the Final Four. Furthermore, 8 of the players from the current roster have been selected by major league teams in the 2007 MLB Draft.</p> 
     <p>School chants and cheers feature the word &quot;zot&quot; which was the noise Johnny Hart's &quot;Peter the Anteater&quot; made while eating ants.</p> 
     <p>A hand signal called &quot;Rip'em 'Eaters&quot; was created by Blake Sasaki and Dennis Wisco in 2001. When attacked, an anteater sits in a tripodal position with its hind feet and tail and tears and &quot;rips&quot; at its predator. The hand signal is done by touching the tips of the two middle fingers with the thumb, and sliding the thumb back, making the pinky and index finger the ears and the fingers in the middle the snout of the anteater.</p> 
     <p>In August 2007, a small stuffed Peter accompanied astronaut <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Caldwell" title="Tracy Caldwell" class="mw-redirect">Tracy Caldwell</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">Space Shuttle <i>Endeavour</i></a> mission <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">STS-118</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Controversy">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/UCI_Medical_Center" title="UCI Medical Center" class="mw-redirect">UCI Medical Center</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aramark">Aramark</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Aramark">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UC Irvine is the last UC campus that <a href="/wiki/Subcontract" title="Subcontract" class="mw-redirect">subcontracts</a> its food services. In summer of 2004, UCI signed a contract with <a href="/wiki/Aramark" title="Aramark">Aramark</a>, a food services corporation, granting it control of nearly all residential dining facilities and restaurants on university property. This includes UCI's three dining halls (Brandywine, Pippin Commons, and Mesa Commons) and three on-campus restaurants (Phoenix Grille, B.C.'s Cavern on the Green, and Bistro by the Bridge). <a href="/wiki/Student_activities_and_traditions_at_UC_Irvine" title="Student activities and traditions at UC Irvine">ASUCI</a>, which is partially responsible for negotiating UCI's food services contract, has justified the decision to offer Aramark its business with the argument that Aramark has pledged to invest millions of dollars into the university's food service infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-Ong_Hing_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ong_Hing-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_school_dean">Law school dean</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Law school dean">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In hiring an inaugural dean of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Irvine_School_of_Law" title="University of California, Irvine School of Law">UC Irvine School of Law</a>, which opened in 2009, the University approached Professor <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Chemerinsky" title="Erwin Chemerinsky">Erwin Chemerinsky</a>, a well known legal scholar in constitutional law and liberal commentator. After signing a contract with Chemerinsky on September 4, 2007, the hire was rescinded by UCI Chancellor Michael V. Drake because he felt the law professor's commentaries were &quot;polarizing&quot; and would not serve the interests of California's first new public law school in 40 years; Drake claimed the decision was his own and not the subject of any outside influence.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT091307a_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT091307a-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> The action was roundly criticized by liberal and conservative scholars who felt it hindered the academic mission of the law school, and disbelief over Chancellor Drake's claims that it was the subject of no outside influence.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT091307a_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT091307a-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LAT901307b_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT901307b-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The issue was the subject of a <a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times" class="mw-redirect">New York Times</a> editorial on September 14, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> Details emerged revealing that UCI had received criticism on the hire from <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_California" title="Supreme Court of California">California Chief Justice</a> <a href="/wiki/Ronald_M._George" title="Ronald M. George">Ronald M. George</a>, who criticized Chemerinsky's grasp of death penalty appeals as well as a group of prominent Orange County Republicans and Los Angeles County Supervisor <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Antonovich" title="Michael D. Antonovich">Michael D. Antonovich</a>, who wanted to derail the appointment.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT901707_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT901707-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Drake traveled over a weekend to <a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">Durham, North Carolina</a>, and the two reached an agreement late Sunday evening.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT901707_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT901707-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> On September 17, Chemerinsky issued a joint press release with UCI Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Michael_V._Drake" title="Michael V. Drake">Michael V. Drake</a> indicating that Chemerinsky <i>would</i> head the UCI law school, stating &quot;Our new law school will be founded on the bedrock principle of academic freedom. The chancellor reiterated his lifelong, unqualified commitment to academic freedom, which extends to every faculty member, including deans and other senior administrators.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-PressRelease070917_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PressRelease070917-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UCI_Extension">UCI Extension</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: UCI Extension">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>From 2002 to 2007, <a href="/wiki/Capella_University" title="Capella University">Capella University</a>, a for-profit, on-line institution, paid $500 per student to UCI Extension for each of the 36 students who transferred to Capella. This undisclosed financial arrangement resulted in a total payment of $12,000 to UCI.<sup id="cite_ref-payment_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-payment-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The payments, first reported in the <i><a href="/wiki/Chronicle_of_Higher_Education" title="Chronicle of Higher Education" class="mw-redirect">Chronicle of Higher Education</a></i>, were inadvertently revealed when Jeffry La Marca, a former student of UCI Extension and Capella, filed a <a href="/wiki/Public_records" title="Public records">public records</a> request for correspondence between UCI and Capella.</p> 
     <p>UCI continuing education dean Gary Matkin announced the school would end the arrangement by October 31, 2007 and plans to place $12,000 into a scholarship fund for needy students. UCI officials represented that the agreement was legal per Department of Education regulations, however, UCI had tried to hide the payments and the arrangement was frequently criticized as unethical because it raised the possibility that school counselors might make recommendations to students based on financial incentives rather than the student's best interests.<sup id="cite_ref-payment_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-payment-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_antisemitism">Allegations of antisemitism</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Allegations of antisemitism">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>On November 30, 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Civil_Rights" title="Office of Civil Rights" class="mw-redirect">Office of Civil Rights</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Education" title="United States Department of Education">United States Department of Education</a> issued a report finding &quot;insufficient evidence&quot; in support of allegations that Jewish students at UCI were harassed and subjected to a hostile environment based on their national origin. The federal agency investigated a total of 13 alleged incidents of harassment that occurred between Fall 2000 and December 2006, and determined that 5 were &quot;isolated acts&quot; that could not be addressed because they were reported more than 180 days after they occurred. Further, the agency considered these acts, which included a rock thrown at a Jewish student, the destruction of a <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust" class="mw-redirect">Holocaust</a> memorial display, and various threatening or harassing statements made to individual Jewish students, substantially different in nature as to be unrelated to the 8 other recurring acts it investigated, which included graffiti depicting <a href="/wiki/Swastika" title="Swastika">swastikas</a> on campus, events during an annual Zionist Awareness Week (in which several Jewish students had, however, partook), exclusion of Jewish students during an anti-hate rally, and the wearing of graduation stoles signifying support for <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a><sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> or <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> human rights. The agency ultimately found that none of the incidents leading to the allegations qualified as &quot;sufficiently severe, pervasive or persistent as to interfere with or limit the ability of an individual to participate in from the services, activities or privileges&quot; provided by UCI, and that university officials had acted appropriately in response to each incident. In December 2007, UCI Administration has been cleared of anti-semitism complaints by the US Department of Education's Office for Civil Rights.<sup id="cite_ref-OCR_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OCR-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Following a speech by Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Michael_V._Drake" title="Michael V. Drake">Michael Drake</a> at the national Hillel meeting in Washington, D.C. in March 2008, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Anteaters_for_Israel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Anteaters for Israel (page does not exist)">Anteaters for Israel</a>, along with three other Jewish organizations, issued a press release defending Drake and claiming that anti-Semitic activity was &quot;exaggerated.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Since then, 20 current and former students issued a statement expressing concern over ongoing issues and Drake's handling of them.</p> 
     <p>In May 2009, UC Irvine hosted a two-week event titled &quot;Israel: The Politics of Genocide&quot;, hosted by the school's Muslim Student Union. Scheduled speakers included <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_McKinney" title="Cynthia McKinney">Cynthia McKinney</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Galloway" title="George Galloway">George Galloway</a>. Opponents of the event described it as &quot;anti-Semitic&quot; (despite its considerable support from Jewish students and stated criticism solely of Israeli policy) and have called for Chancellor Drake to condemn both the event and the sponsoring organization. He has declined to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> One outdoor demonstration at this event included a display with an image of Jewish Holocaust victim <a href="/wiki/Anne_Frank" title="Anne Frank">Anne Frank</a> wearing a <a href="/wiki/Keffiyah" title="Keffiyah" class="mw-redirect">keffiyah</a>, in an apparent attempt to draw an analogy between her sufferings and the plight of the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinians</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestinian territories</a>. The pro-Israel campus advocacy group <a href="/wiki/StandWithUs" title="StandWithUs">StandWithUs</a> has described this image as offensive.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In October 2009, students from UCI met with <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> official <a href="/wiki/Aziz_Duwaik" title="Aziz Duwaik">Aziz Duwaik</a> on a university-sponsored trip to the West Bank under a program called the Olive Tree Initiative (OTI), a neutral, apolitical education group that studies the Arab-Israeli conflict. The meeting was questioned by parties in 2011, and the initial response from UCI was that the meeting was justified, as the education group was studying the different narratives that contribute to the current situation in the middle east.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Zionist_Organization_of_America" title="Zionist Organization of America">Zionist Organization of America</a> informed UCI about Hamas' nature and urged UCI to dissociate itself from the OTI, UCI referred to the meeting as a &quot;misstep.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of these accusations were contradicted by many organizations and members of the group who are of pro-Israel and Jewish descent.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In May, 2010, forty members of the faculty issued an open letter expressing concern about &quot;hate-promoting actions&quot; including &quot;a statement (by a speaker repeatedly invited by the Muslim Student Union) that the Zionist Jew is a party of Satan, a statement by another MSU speaker that the Holocaust was God?s will&quot; that have given UCI &quot;a growing reputation as a center of hate and intolerance.&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Neither of the speakers had been named nor any students shown to have had any affiliation with such remarks.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrests_at_Michael_Oren_lecture">Arrests at Michael Oren lecture</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Arrests at Michael Oren lecture">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UC Irvine attracted controversy in February 2010 when students disrupted a lecture by Israeli Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Michael_Oren" title="Michael Oren">Michael Oren</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Suspends_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suspends-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> While the MSU had issued a statement condemning the university for inviting a man who ?took part in a culture that has no qualms with terrorizing the innocent, killing civilians, demolishing their homes and illegally occupying their land,? they denied responsibility for the protests and said the students acted on their own.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Stern" title="Kenneth Stern" class="mw-redirect">Kenneth Stern</a>, director of the <a href="/wiki/American_Jewish_Committee" title="American Jewish Committee">American Jewish Committee</a>'s Division on Antisemitism and Extremism &quot;The UCI campus has had a long history of anti-Israel and anti-Semitic incidents, usually tied to its Muslim Student Union.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Heckler" title="Heckler">Hecklers</a> interrupted Oren's speech 10 times with many students cheering them in support. Among other slogans, the hecklers yelled, &quot;Michael Oren, propagating murder is not an expression of <a href="/wiki/Free_speech" title="Free speech" class="mw-redirect">free speech</a>,&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> &quot;killers&quot; and &quot;how many Palestinians did you kill?&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> After the fourth disruption, Oren took a 20-minute leave before returning to the podium. Before continuing he said, &quot;I?ve spent most of my life living in and studying the Middle East and one of the great and eternal cultural facets of the Middle East is hospitality...even if you do not agree with them, even if they?re ostensibly your enemy. I?m your guest here and I?m asking for the Middle Eastern hospitality for your guest, I?ve come into your house.&quot; By the end of the program, 11 UC Irvine and <a href="/wiki/UC_Riverside" title="UC Riverside" class="mw-redirect">Riverside</a> students were reportedly arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to <a href="/wiki/New_University_(newspaper)" title="New University (newspaper)">New University</a> newspaper, 11 students were charged with section 403 of the UCIPD penal code ? disrupting a public event on the University?s property, for their actions. Nine were enrolled at UCI and three were from UCR.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>During the event, UCI Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Michael_V._Drake" title="Michael V. Drake">Michael Drake</a> and political science department chair Mark Petracca &quot;chided the protesting crowd and called the disruptions embarrassing.&quot; At one point, Chairman Petracca yelled &quot;Shame on you&quot; to the heckling crowd.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_97-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> In a statement issued the next day, UCI Chancellor Drake called the students' behavior &quot;intolerable,&quot; saying that &quot;Freedom of speech is among the most fundamental, and among the most cherished of the bedrock values our nation is built upon.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> UCI Law School Dean <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Chemerinsky" title="Erwin Chemerinsky">Erwin Chemerinsky</a> also condemned the disruptions. He stated, &quot;Imagine if they had brought their own speaker and that person had been shouted down. There would be no free speech. There is no right to a ?<a href="/wiki/Heckler%27s_veto" title="Heckler's veto">heckler?s veto</a>.?&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In response, the university suspended the group for the 2010?2011 school year and the group will undergo a probationary period for the following year. In addition, the members will be responsible for completing a collective 50 community service hours before the group can be reinstated. The <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Student_Union" title="Muslim Student Union" class="mw-redirect">Muslim Student Union</a> has appealed the suspension.<sup id="cite_ref-Suspends_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suspends-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The punishment was later modified to one academic quarter, one hundred hours of community service, and two years probation.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Zionist_Organization_of_America" title="Zionist Organization of America">Zionist Organization of America</a>, describing UCI as &quot;a campus that permitted bigotry&quot;, has called for college-bound students and financial donors to avoid UCI.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Irvine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Notable alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_California,_Irvine_people" title="List of University of California, Irvine people">List of University of California, Irvine people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>As of 2011, UCI has more than 124,000 alumni.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> As with any major university, many UC Irvine alumni have achieved fame after graduating. These people include athletes (<a href="/wiki/Steve_Scott_(athlete)" title="Steve Scott (athlete)">Steve Scott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Brooks" title="Scott Brooks">Scott Brooks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greg_Louganis" title="Greg Louganis">Greg Louganis</a> and 34 Olympians), Broadway, film, and television actors (<a href="/wiki/Bob_Gunton" title="Bob Gunton">Bob Gunton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Lovitz" title="Jon Lovitz">Jon Lovitz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Thompson" title="Brian Thompson">Brian Thompson</a>), and technological innovators (<a href="/wiki/Roy_Fielding" title="Roy Fielding">Roy Fielding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Mockapetris" title="Paul Mockapetris">Paul Mockapetris</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Patrick_J._Hanratty" title="Patrick J. Hanratty">Patrick J. Hanratty</a><sup id="cite_ref-UC_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UC-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup>).</p> 
     <p>The UC Irvine writing program has produced a number of authors, such as <a href="/wiki/Michael_Chabon" title="Michael Chabon">Michael Chabon</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_L._McMichael" title="James L. McMichael">James McMichael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Carlson" title="Ron Carlson">Ron Carlson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Peters" title="Robert Peters">Robert Peters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alice_Sebold" title="Alice Sebold">Alice Sebold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aimee_Bender" title="Aimee Bender">Aimee Bender</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Ford" title="Richard Ford">Richard Ford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yusef_Komunyakaa" title="Yusef Komunyakaa">Yusef Komunyakaa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marti_Leimbach" title="Marti Leimbach">Marti Leimbach</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Whitney_Otto&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Whitney Otto (page does not exist)">Whitney Otto</a> and <a href="/wiki/T._Jefferson_Parker" title="T. Jefferson Parker">T. Jefferson Parker</a>. The renown of these writers has contributed to the national reputation of the school's creative writing program. More recent alumni include <a href="/wiki/Glen_David_Gold" title="Glen David Gold">Glen David Gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maile_Meloy" title="Maile Meloy">Maile Meloy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Espinoza" title="Alex Espinoza">Alex Espinoza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Ferris" title="Joshua Ferris">Joshua Ferris</a>.</p> 
     <p>Several members of the faculty have been honored with the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer</a>. In 1995, two UCI Professors earned the Nobel Prize:<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dr._Frank_Sherwood_Rowland" title="Dr. Frank Sherwood Rowland" class="mw-redirect">Dr. Frank Sherwood Rowland</a> won in chemistry and <a href="/wiki/Dr._Frederick_Reines" title="Dr. Frederick Reines" class="mw-redirect">Dr. Frederick Reines</a> won in physics. In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Irwin_Rose" title="Dr. Irwin Rose" class="mw-redirect">Dr. Irwin Rose</a> earned UCI its third Nobel, this time in chemistry. <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ramirez" title="Michael Ramirez">Michael Ramirez</a> is a two-time <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>-winning American editorial cartoonist and a Senior Editor for <a href="/wiki/Investor%27s_Business_Daily" title="Investor's Business Daily">Investor's Business Daily</a>.</p> 
     <p>Claude Yarbrough (aka <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Pendragon" title="Jonathan Pendragon" class="mw-redirect">Jonathan Pendragon</a>), class of '76, is one of the most influential magicians of the 20th and 21st centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Ralph Cicerone, an earth system science professor and former chancellor, is currently president of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Faculty members who have taught literary criticism and critical theory at UCI have included <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Derrida" title="Jacques Derrida">Jacques Derrida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murray_Krieger" title="Murray Krieger">Murray Krieger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Iser" title="Wolfgang Iser">Wolfgang Iser</a>, and visiting professors in these fields have included <a href="/wiki/Judith_Butler" title="Judith Butler">Judith Butler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavoj_%C5%BDi%C5%BEek" title="Slavoj ?i?ek">Slavoj ?i?ek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Agamben" title="Giorgio Agamben">Giorgio Agamben</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Johnson" title="Barbara Johnson">Barbara Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fredric_Jameson" title="Fredric Jameson">Fredric Jameson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Grosz" title="Elizabeth Grosz">Elizabeth Grosz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Balibar" title="&Eacute;tienne Balibar">&Eacute;tienne Balibar</a>.</p> 
     <p>Movie directors who attended UCI include <a href="/wiki/Joseph_McGinty_Nichol" title="Joseph McGinty Nichol" class="mw-redirect">McG</a>, and Robert Beaucage, director of <i><a href="/wiki/Spike_(2008_film)" title="Spike (2008 film)">Spike</a></i>.</p>
